{"uri": "8209739769", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-04", "time": "14:49:29", "dateTime": "2024-07-04T14:49:29Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-04T14:49:07Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9372549057006836, "url": "https://pressofatlanticcity.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/music/woodstock-bethel-baby-boomers-new-york/article_41a5447c-47d3-5de8-ba5e-1faa29734ab0.html", "title": "Back to Woodstock, with Wi-Fi: Women return after 55 years to glamp and relive the famous festival", "body": "BETHEL, N.Y. -- Beverly \"Cookie\" Grant hitchhiked to the Woodstock music festival in 1969 without a ticket and slept on straw. Ellen Shelburne arrived in a VW microbus and pitched a pup tent.\n\nFifty-five years later, the two longtime friends finally got back to the garden, but this time in high style.\n\nThe women, now 76, were recently treated to a two-bedroom glamping tent at the upstate New York site equipped with comfy beds, a shower, a coffee maker and Wi-Fi. No mud from drenching rains this time. They sat in pavilion seats to watch shows by Woodstock veterans John Fogerty and Roger Daltrey.\n\n\"We're like hippie queens!\" Grant joked over breakfast during the trip earlier this month.\n\nThe Bethel Woods Center for the Arts, the not-for-profit organization that runs the site, rolled out the tie-dyed carpet for Grant and Shelburne to promote its new luxury camping -- or glamping -- facilities and to delve deeper into Shelburne's trove of photos from the generation-defining festival held Aug. 15-18, 1969.\n\nPeople are also reading... Atlantic City Beer and Music Festival canceled Nine rescued from waters off Ninth Street beach in Ocean City Wildwood: No more 'dog days' on the Boardwalk this summer Former site for Sister Jean's, 'Nucky' Johnson wedding to be demolished to make way for cannabis business Chicken Guy! restaurant debuts Tuesday in Atlantic City Water main break repaired in Wildwood Ousted Atlantic City school board member sues, alleging retaliation, racial discrimination Cape May Carriage horse dies on the job Your guide to Fourth of July fireworks in South Jersey Rain can't keep thousands away from Wildwood beach soccer tournament Galloway woman charged with 43 counts of neglect after multiple dead animals found at home 17-year-old dies in fatal Dennis Township crash Man found dead on Wildwood Crest beach NBA star Jalen Brunson, rapper Flavor Flav spotted in Atlantic City After an influential career, Mike Gatley steps down as Mainland Regional athletic director\n\nThe once-trampled hillside by the main stage is now a manicured green space near a Woodstock-and-'60s-themed museum and the concert pavilion. But the return visit still bought back a flood of memories. Shelburne was able to retrace the steps she took as a 21-year-old college student in the photos taken by her then-boyfriend, and future husband, David Shelburne.\n\n\"I'm looking at this person in the photograph, who is me, but a person just starting out in life at that age. And now I'm looking back at sort of bookends of my life,\" Ellen Shelburne said. \"All these decades later, I'm back at Woodstock and it just brings it all up in such a positive way.\"\n\nGrant and Shelburne did not know each other in August 1969 and they attended the concert separately.\n\nShelburne came from Columbus, Ohio, with David Shelburne, his best friend and another woman. They purchased tickets, got there early and bought ponchos at a local store after rain was forecast. She slept in a pup tent.\n\n\"I was never cold, wet, hungry, muddy, dirty, uncomfortable or miserable,\" she said. \"It was the total opposite.\"\n\nGrant went to Woodstock on a lark.\n\nA long-haired surfer she knew named Ray came up to her and a friend on a beach in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, and said, \"There's this music festival happening in New York. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site Be the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "pressofatlanticcity.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Press of Atlantic City"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@pressofatlanticcity.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site 0 Comments Love 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "magicvalley.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Magic Valley"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@magicvalley.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": true}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. {"uri": "8209727427", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-04", "time": "14:40:43", "dateTime": "2024-07-04T14:40:43Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-04T14:40:20Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9254902005195618, "url": "https://journalstar.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/music/woodstock-bethel-baby-boomers-new-york/article_e8460f67-e11e-5b56-80c0-3805e3168679.html", "title": "Back to Woodstock, with Wi-Fi: Women return after 55 years to glamp and relive the famous festival", "body": "BETHEL, N.Y. -- Beverly \"Cookie\" Grant hitchhiked to the Woodstock music festival in 1969 without a ticket and slept on straw. Ellen Shelburne arrived in a VW microbus and pitched a pup tent.\n\nFifty-five years later, the two longtime friends finally got back to the garden, but this time in high style.\n\nThe women, now 76, were recently treated to a two-bedroom glamping tent at the upstate New York site equipped with comfy beds, a shower, a coffee maker and Wi-Fi. No mud from drenching rains this time. They sat in pavilion seats to watch shows by Woodstock veterans John Fogerty and Roger Daltrey.\n\n\"We're like hippie queens!\" Grant joked over breakfast during the trip earlier this month.\n\nThe Bethel Woods Center for the Arts, the not-for-profit organization that runs the site, rolled out the tie-dyed carpet for Grant and Shelburne to promote its new luxury camping -- or glamping -- facilities and to delve deeper into Shelburne's trove of photos from the generation-defining festival held Aug. 15-18, 1969.\n\nPeople are also reading... North Lincoln grain elevator will soon come down after it was purchased at auction Crete, Nebraska: 7 shot in 'welcoming community' by neighbor who 'hated everybody' Lincoln in flood warning, more severe storms possible Tuesday afternoon 6 people injured in Crete shooting; suspect dead, State Patrol says 74-year-old identified as gunman in Crete shooting that injured 7 DJ Diesel, aka Shaq, draws superstar-sized crowd to Lincoln nightclub 'Let us in' -- Concertgoers voice frustrations after large crowd packed Royal Grove to see Shaq Baker's Candies store in Greenwood to double in size with multimillion-dollar expansion America's first official 'quiet trail' sits in the Nebraska Sandhills Lincoln's wind turbines blown up in northeast Lincoln Lincoln's Uncle Sam Jam celebration will now include food vendors Drivers will face nighttime detours on I-80 west of Lincoln this week Garner Industries relocates in Lincoln after tornado destroys plant Heavy rain causes flash flooding in Lincoln Omaha Supernovas sign 3 former Nebraska volleyball players\n\nThe once-trampled hillside by the main stage is now a manicured green space near a Woodstock-and-'60s-themed museum and the concert pavilion. But the return visit still bought back a flood of memories. Shelburne was able to retrace the steps she took as a 21-year-old college student in the photos taken by her then-boyfriend, and future husband, David Shelburne.\n\n\"I'm looking at this person in the photograph, who is me, but a person just starting out in life at that age. And now I'm looking back at sort of bookends of my life,\" Ellen Shelburne said. \"All these decades later, I'm back at Woodstock and it just brings it all up in such a positive way.\"\n\nGrant and Shelburne did not know each other in August 1969 and they attended the concert separately.\n\nShelburne came from Columbus, Ohio, with David Shelburne, his best friend and another woman. They purchased tickets, got there early and bought ponchos at a local store after rain was forecast. She slept in a pup tent.\n\n\"I was never cold, wet, hungry, muddy, dirty, uncomfortable or miserable,\" she said. \"It was the total opposite.\"\n\nGrant went to Woodstock on a lark.\n\nA long-haired surfer she knew named Ray came up to her and a friend on a beach in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, and said, \"There's this music festival happening in New York. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site 0 Comments Love 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "journalstar.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "JournalStar.com"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@journalstar.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}, {"uri": "julia_nikhinson@journalstar.com", "name": "Julia Nikhinson", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. {"uri": "8209713713", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-04", "time": "14:31:02", "dateTime": "2024-07-04T14:31:02Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-04T14:30:41Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9176470637321472, "url": "https://theeagle.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/music/woodstock-bethel-baby-boomers-new-york/article_34f05cb4-fdf4-5f82-b5fb-42038e859ba0.html", "title": "Back to Woodstock, with Wi-Fi: Women return after 55 years to glamp and relive the famous festival", "body": "BETHEL, N.Y. -- Beverly \"Cookie\" Grant hitchhiked to the Woodstock music festival in 1969 without a ticket and slept on straw. Ellen Shelburne arrived in a VW microbus and pitched a pup tent.\n\nFifty-five years later, the two longtime friends finally got back to the garden, but this time in high style.\n\nThe women, now 76, were recently treated to a two-bedroom glamping tent at the upstate New York site equipped with comfy beds, a shower, a coffee maker and Wi-Fi. No mud from drenching rains this time. They sat in pavilion seats to watch shows by Woodstock veterans John Fogerty and Roger Daltrey.\n\n\"We're like hippie queens!\" Grant joked over breakfast during the trip earlier this month.\n\nThe Bethel Woods Center for the Arts, the not-for-profit organization that runs the site, rolled out the tie-dyed carpet for Grant and Shelburne to promote its new luxury camping -- or glamping -- facilities and to delve deeper into Shelburne's trove of photos from the generation-defining festival held Aug. 15-18, 1969.\n\nPeople are also reading... Texas A&M hires Washington head baseball coach Jason Kelly as pitching coach Even without college coaches, Texas A&M baseball camps must go on Texas A&M AD Trev Alberts details days leading up to Jim Schlossnagle's departure Watch: Jace LaViolette explains decision to stay at Texas A&M Bryan child dies in lightning strike, family starts GoFundMe Texas A&M hires Michael Earley as head baseball coach Bryan family settles into new house from Habitat for Humanity 'This is my home': Jace LaViolette, Gavin Grahovac announce they will return to Texas A&M Cessna: Scorned Aggies need to make Schlossnagle regret his move New Texas A&M baseball coach Michael Earley can teach hitting, but relationships is where he thrives Texas A&M baseball team set to compete in 2025 Astros Foundation College Classic Texas A&M Chancellor John Sharp announces he will retire in a year Texas A&M baseball team announces annual team awards Waco man arrested in Brazos County for alleged theft of a firearm Texas A&M infielder Kaeden Kent to return to Aggie baseball program\n\nThe once-trampled hillside by the main stage is now a manicured green space near a Woodstock-and-'60s-themed museum and the concert pavilion. But the return visit still bought back a flood of memories. Shelburne was able to retrace the steps she took as a 21-year-old college student in the photos taken by her then-boyfriend, and future husband, David Shelburne.\n\n\"I'm looking at this person in the photograph, who is me, but a person just starting out in life at that age. And now I'm looking back at sort of bookends of my life,\" Ellen Shelburne said. \"All these decades later, I'm back at Woodstock and it just brings it all up in such a positive way.\"\n\nGrant and Shelburne did not know each other in August 1969 and they attended the concert separately.\n\nShelburne came from Columbus, Ohio, with David Shelburne, his best friend and another woman. They purchased tickets, got there early and bought ponchos at a local store after rain was forecast. She slept in a pup tent.\n\n\"I was never cold, wet, hungry, muddy, dirty, uncomfortable or miserable,\" she said. \"It was the total opposite.\"\n\nGrant went to Woodstock on a lark.\n\nA long-haired surfer she knew named Ray came up to her and a friend on a beach in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, and said, \"There's this music festival happening in New York. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site Be the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "theeagle.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "The Eagle"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@theeagle.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site 0 Comments Be the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "missoulian.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "missoulian.com"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@missoulian.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. {"uri": "8209728978", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-04", "time": "14:41:40", "dateTime": "2024-07-04T14:41:40Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-04T14:41:17Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9137254953384399, "url": "https://statesville.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/music/woodstock-bethel-baby-boomers-new-york/article_e36b015c-3469-5b8b-8157-9d49b5db8924.html", "title": "Back to Woodstock, with Wi-Fi: Women return after 55 years to glamp and relive the famous festival", "body": "BETHEL, N.Y. -- Beverly \"Cookie\" Grant hitchhiked to the Woodstock music festival in 1969 without a ticket and slept on straw. Ellen Shelburne arrived in a VW microbus and pitched a pup tent.\n\nFifty-five years later, the two longtime friends finally got back to the garden, but this time in high style.\n\nThe women, now 76, were recently treated to a two-bedroom glamping tent at the upstate New York site equipped with comfy beds, a shower, a coffee maker and Wi-Fi. No mud from drenching rains this time. They sat in pavilion seats to watch shows by Woodstock veterans John Fogerty and Roger Daltrey.\n\n\"We're like hippie queens!\" Grant joked over breakfast during the trip earlier this month.\n\nThe Bethel Woods Center for the Arts, the not-for-profit organization that runs the site, rolled out the tie-dyed carpet for Grant and Shelburne to promote its new luxury camping -- or glamping -- facilities and to delve deeper into Shelburne's trove of photos from the generation-defining festival held Aug. 15-18, 1969.\n\nPeople are also reading... Iredell chase ends with crash; one reported dead Statesville planning board OKs development with at least 900 homes Former Greyhound Stevenson eager to play again for Wake Forest after recovering from ACL tear Fayetteville man charged in fatal Iredell County wreck Iredell EMS deputy director talks about his termination. Appeal set for July 10 Harwell picked again to be umpire in charge for Babe Ruth World Series games US Marshals nab Statesville man wanted in fatal April shooting North Carolina Public health restaurant and food-stand inspections in Iredell County, June 14-27 Troutman Independence Day Parade starts holiday early Iredell County to host meeting regarding proposed new convenience center Iredell Health honors long-serving employees: Keith Williams started career at IMH and hopes to end it there Mooresville man convicted of murder at 14 suing state official over denied parole Statesville's Outstanding Teen captures state crown Fugitive captured in Troutman, returned to Pennsylvania by airplane Statesville motorcyclist killed in crash near Mooresville Wednesday\n\nThe once-trampled hillside by the main stage is now a manicured green space near a Woodstock-and-'60s-themed museum and the concert pavilion. But the return visit still bought back a flood of memories. Shelburne was able to retrace the steps she took as a 21-year-old college student in the photos taken by her then-boyfriend, and future husband, David Shelburne.\n\n\"I'm looking at this person in the photograph, who is me, but a person just starting out in life at that age. And now I'm looking back at sort of bookends of my life,\" Ellen Shelburne said. \"All these decades later, I'm back at Woodstock and it just brings it all up in such a positive way.\"\n\nGrant and Shelburne did not know each other in August 1969 and they attended the concert separately.\n\nShelburne came from Columbus, Ohio, with David Shelburne, his best friend and another woman. They purchased tickets, got there early and bought ponchos at a local store after rain was forecast. She slept in a pup tent.\n\n\"I was never cold, wet, hungry, muddy, dirty, uncomfortable or miserable,\" she said. \"It was the total opposite.\"\n\nGrant went to Woodstock on a lark.\n\nA long-haired surfer she knew named Ray came up to her and a friend on a beach in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, and said, \"There's this music festival happening in New York. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site Be the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that registration on or use of this site constitutes agreement to its user agreement and privacy policy.", "source": {"uri": "statesville.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Statesville.com"}, "authors": [{"uri": "associated_press@statesville.com", "name": "Associated Press", "type": "author", "isAgency": false}], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glamping", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Glamping"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Ulysses S. {"uri": "8209767606", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-04", "time": "15:09:54", "dateTime": "2024-07-04T15:09:54Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-04T15:08:06Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8980392217636108, "url": "https://tucson.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/music/woodstock-bethel-baby-boomers-new-york/article_e93cb7ce-ccd7-5c40-88c8-a02ca9ede848.html", "title": "Back to Woodstock, with Wi-Fi: Women return after 55 years to glamp and relive the famous festival", "body": "BETHEL, N.Y. -- Beverly \"Cookie\" Grant hitchhiked to the Woodstock music festival in 1969 without a ticket and slept on straw. Ellen Shelburne arrived in a VW microbus and pitched a pup tent.\n\nFifty-five years later, the two longtime friends finally got back to the garden, but this time in high style.\n\nThe women, now 76, were recently treated to a two-bedroom glamping tent at the upstate New York site equipped with comfy beds, a shower, a coffee maker and Wi-Fi. No mud from drenching rains this time. They sat in pavilion seats to watch shows by Woodstock veterans John Fogerty and Roger Daltrey.\n\n\"We're like hippie queens!\" Grant joked over breakfast during the trip earlier this month.\n\nThe Bethel Woods Center for the Arts, the not-for-profit organization that runs the site, rolled out the tie-dyed carpet for Grant and Shelburne to promote its new luxury camping -- or glamping -- facilities and to delve deeper into Shelburne's trove of photos from the generation-defining festival held Aug. 15-18, 1969.\n\nPeople are also reading... A rare classic car museum is expanding at a new Tucson location Rise in drivers behaving badly across metro Tucson grabs police attention Iconic Tucson bar expanding to Phoenix Don't sleep on the carne asada from The Quesadillas, which might be one of Tucson's best-kept secrets Tornado touches down in Tucson, officials confirm Monsoon is here! 9 Tucson restaurants and bars to watch the weather Arizona, Tucson actions on homeless may follow Supreme Court ruling Arizona firm named in Justice Department's $2.7B health care fraud crackdown Where to watch fireworks in Tucson this Fourth of July Take your pick from these Tucson-area Fourth of July fireworks shows 35 fun events happening in Tucson this weekend June 27-30 \ud83c\udf9e\ud83d\udc10 34 fun events happening in Tucson this weekend ESPN projects four Arizona Wildcats to be taken in 2025 NBA Draft Guiding a modern-day basketball 'Dream Team,' Steve Kerr aims to avoid a nightmare at Paris Olympics Tucson police: Siblings dead in apparent murder-suicide\n\nThe once-trampled hillside by the main stage is now a manicured green space near a Woodstock-and-'60s-themed museum and the concert pavilion. But the return visit still bought back a flood of memories. Shelburne was able to retrace the steps she took as a 21-year-old college student in the photos taken by her then-boyfriend, and future husband, David Shelburne.\n\n\"I'm looking at this person in the photograph, who is me, but a person just starting out in life at that age. And now I'm looking back at sort of bookends of my life,\" Ellen Shelburne said. \"All these decades later, I'm back at Woodstock and it just brings it all up in such a positive way.\"\n\nGrant and Shelburne did not know each other in August 1969 and they attended the concert separately.\n\nShelburne came from Columbus, Ohio, with David Shelburne, his best friend and another woman. They purchased tickets, got there early and bought ponchos at a local store after rain was forecast. She slept in a pup tent.\n\n\"I was never cold, wet, hungry, muddy, dirty, uncomfortable or miserable,\" she said. \"It was the total opposite.\"\n\nGrant went to Woodstock on a lark.\n\nA long-haired surfer she knew named Ray came up to her and a friend on a beach in Fort Lauderdale, Florida, and said, \"There's this music festival happening in New York. You want to hitchhike up there with me?\" Grant's friend dropped out along the way, but she and the surfer made it to the town of Bethel. The last driver dropped them off at the edge of the epic traffic jam outside the festival and gave them a blanket.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack\n\nGrant walked the last several miles to Woodstock barefoot.\n\nBoth women were wowed by Jimi Hendrix, The Who and other musical acts, but also by the good vibes from the 400,000 or more people who converged on Max Yasgur's dairy farm some 80 miles northwest of New York City.\n\n\"If we needed food, someone gave us food. Someone gave us water. We needed nothing,\" Grant said.\n\nThe two women met months later in Columbus, where they each ran shops adjacent to Ohio State University with the men they went to Woodstock with. And they each married their concert companions, though Grant got a divorce several years later.\n\nDavid and Ellen Shelburne ran a film and video production company together until he died four years ago. Grant moved to Florida and eventually became a chef on mega-yachts before starting her own business providing crews for those big boats.\n\nEach woman kept a spark of the Woodstock spirit. Shelburne said she's \"stuck in the '60s and proud of it.\" They got the bug to return to the festival site last year after providing oral histories in Columbus to curators for the Museum at Bethel Woods.\n\nJust like in 1969, the women were provided what they needed during their recent long weekend of peace, love and nostalgia -- though this time it was a \"Luxury 2 Bedroom Safari Tent\" with a front deck and the shower in a bathroom. And when it rained this time, they were able to stay dry in the museum.\n\nOn a sunny Saturday, Bethel Woods senior curator Neal Hitch drove the women around in a golf cart to explore the spots where David Shelburne shot his festival photos. Unlike others who focused their cameras on the stage, he documented festivalgoers camping, swimming, selling goods, relaxing and having fun. Hitch noted that David Shelburne's images also are valuable because they are in sequence, meaning they tell a story.\n\nAt one stop, Shelburne stood by a tree line as she held a photo of a field full of campers. She was standing on the spot where her late husband took the photograph and was looking at the same field, minus the campers, 55 years later. Visibly moved, she said \"oh\" a few times and let out a deep breath before exclaiming, \"Wow!\"\n\nIt broke her heart that her husband is not in the photographs, but she felt his presence that weekend.\n\nThe women ranged across the festival site over several days, from the stage area to the woods where vendors had set up stalls. Despite the changes -- the luxury tents, the fences, the museum -- the women said they recognized the same mellow, friendly vibes here that they experienced as 21-year-olds.\n\nAnd they were thrilled to immerse themselves in it again decades later.\n\n\"It's very wonderful to see that it's in history forever,\" Grant said, \"and we're a part of that.\"\n\nWoodstock 55 years later: Camping out in luxury at iconic site\n\nSubscribe to stay connected to Tucson.
